B003VANOFY|4.0|I love this headset. It is very sexy and built to last like most of Logitech's products. The best feature is by far that it's wireless. I can literally be 40 feet away from my bedroom upstairs, in my kitchen downstairs and still have a conversation with someone on Skype. The battery lasts around 8 hoursObviously your milage will vary with wireless, so don't expect your house to let you do the same, but overall I think you'll really like the range you'll get form these. Things you'll want to worry about that create interference for wireless use are: multiple wireless networks, 2.4GHz wireless phones, bluetooth devices, a microwave, large metal objects or shielding inside walls, Direct Satellite Service (DSS) radio frequency (RF) leakage, Power lines, railroad tracks and power stations, Pacemakers, Hearing aids, the list goes on. Some great reading on wifi Interference can be found by googling \\"20 Myths of Wi-Fi Interference\\".<br /><br />***Comfort: I'll admit that a headset isn't going to feel like a feather on your head after 3 hours of gaming, or whatever you do when using it. It's big and kinda bulky, but that doesn't bug me. Surprisingly it is very comfortable after prolonged use. If you have longer hair I'd recommend putting into a pony tail while you use these. If you tend to perspire a lot then perhaps use a small desk fan to help. I do perspire and I haven't found these to be a huge contributing factor to it if I make sure that the room I'm playing in is adequately ventilated.<br /><br />***Sound Quality: This is where I feel this product lacks luster. overall the sound is...well...just ok. It suffers most on the low end where a lot of distortion comes through when anything with a lot of bass is played. This is most noticeable in games that have load sounds with low frequencies. Explosions from rag grenades or loud gunshots tend to cause the drivers to bottom out. This can be mitigated by adjusting the EQ settings a little, but I feel that the sound quality of this headset is it's weakest link.<br /><br />***Build Quality: Logitech has used quality parts to build this headset, and it shows because they offer a 2 year warranty on it. If taken care of this could last much longer than just 2 years. Sure something better will be out by then, but it's nice to know that you can depend on a product to last the duration of it's warranty period.<br /><br />***Ease of Use: You'll need a basic understanding of computers to get this working, but if you are a computer enthusiast or even just a casual gamer then I don't think you'll have any issues at all getting things set up. Honestly it is almost plug and play. Just plug it in and install the drivers. The bigest obstacle is making sure that the headset itself is setup as your audio device in windows or in each application you will use independently.<br /><br />***Overall: I feel that for most FPS players these will be a disappointment because the lower end frequencies aren't handled well so you'll get distortion a lot. For those that play RTS or RPGs these are great. It's sad that the biggest group of users (FPS players) will be the ones to deal with the issue of distortion more than others. Tweak it with the EQ settings and it sounds better, but it is still a little disappointing. I feel that when you look at the headset as an entire product it is worth money you'll put out for it.

B002ZG974M|3.0|I couldn't get through this film until I was 4 months pregnant. Otherwise, without dialog, it was too boring. (I found the cats more entertaining to watch.) I'm not one of these people that thinks babies are cute so perhaps if you are, you'll like it more.<br /><br />As a parent-to-be, I found the contrast between the consumer lifestyle of first world countries with third-world countries very interesting. I was also intrigued with other culture's hands-off approach to parenting. But, after watching the movie, I find that it didn't probe these differences enough for me to make a decision about which method is healthier. In fact, it mostly confused the issue. (Some might say that the movie was not trying to indicate one method was better than another... but I think, very subtly, it was definitely criticizing first world methods and presenting the \\"Noble Savage\\" methods as something more respectful.)<br /><br />For instance, in one scene, an African baby takes the toy of his older sibling. The older sibling takes it back. The baby hits him. The older sibling hits back. The baby cries and no one comes to comfort him because no one is watching them. As a viewer, my first reaction was, \\"Well, that will teach the baby not to take toys and hit! I'm glad the mother didn't rush in and scold the older sibling.\\"<br /><br />But, then, later, I watched an older Mongolian toddler full out attack his younger baby brother and no one intervened. He simply kept hitting the baby until he got bored. All the while, the baby was crying. No one came to his rescue. Then, the minute that little baby learned to stand the first thing he did was reach over and grab someone who was smaller than him and made her cry. What had he learned? If you are bigger, you can beat up on those smaller than yourself.<br /><br />So, which is best? Give children less supervision and let them sort it out for themselves, risking that one child will abuse the other, or intervene and risk over-protecting your child?Which is the worse evil? Over protection or a bullied/bullying child? The film did not answer these questions or even probe these questions deeply.<br /><br />Also, I found it a little distasteful that the film makers rushed to make fun of \\"first-worlders\\". The scene where the little girl in Japan had a room full of toys and seemed bored and unhappy was contrasted with the little boy in Mongolia who was tied to a bed and was SOOO happy to get a roll of toilet paper to play with. The message, \\"We give our children too much!\\" was loud and clear throughout the film. But at this point, I thought, \\"WAIT! We don't know if the baby in Japan was bored and unhappy because of her toys. She could simply be overdue for a nap! Also, I bet the boy in Mongolia has similar, cranky, overstimulated days and moments, also!\\" It got me wondering if I was actually being presented with the truth of the situation or with a trendy message about American consumerism.<br /><br />And the little clips of the San Fran couple singing tribal songs about the earth mother with their children while inter cut with clips of the real African tribe... come on! Everybody knows we're suppose to laugh at the stupid Americans at this point. All that did was make me wonder at the agenda of the film-makers and if they were presenting an accurate picture of both American parenting and other culture's.<br /><br />So, was it worth my time to watch as a parent-to-be? Yes. It will definitely make me think more about being too over-protective and too involved in my child's life. But other than as a \\"caution sign\\" in the back of mind, I'm not sure if this film is actually going to change any of my parenting behaviors (I'm still going to buy tons of learning toys because is it better to risk over-stimulating the child, sometimes, or risk under stimulating the baby's brain and s/he lags in development?) So, see it but expect it to confuse you a little bit about how to parent and don't expect it to answer any questions.

Along with the male tribute, Peeta Mellark -- a boy who once helped her at her lowest point -- she is swept away to the Capitol.<br /><br />Once there, the tributes are pampered, tutored, styled and turned into celebrities -- until they're released into the arena, and start killing each other to survive. Katniss must evade murderous gangs, traps, and genetically engineered beasts.<br /><br />But after their triumphant first appearance at the Capitol, the audience has taken a shine to the impoverished young \\"lovers\\" and are rooting for them to triumph. But if both Katniss and Peeta are to survive, they must learn how to play the game that the gamemakers and polticians are playing -- and use the Hunger Games against them.<br /><br />A lot has been made of \\"The Hunger Games'\\" resemblance to the Japanese franchise \\"Battle Royale,\\" but honestly the only real similarity is the core concept. Suzanne Collins' world is a far stranger place, set in a futuristic North America where rebellion is brewing against a tyrant. And it seems more to be a barbed, glass-sharp satire on reality TV and how easily people are swayed, either for evil or good.<br /><br />Suzanne Collins' writing style here takes a little getting used to -- she not only writes everything in the first person, but in the present tense. It's.... a little strange, and it takes some getting used to.<br /><br />But once you do get used to the odd style, Collins' writing is on fire. She writes in an intense, slow-burning style that is speckled with bittersweet scenes (Katniss singing to Rue) and colorful descriptions (the superficial, sparkly Capitol). But it's also brutally violent at times, with various teens being killed in some truly gruesome ways (broken neck, countless stings, arrows) -- and though Collins doesn't go into graphic detail, it's still pretty shocking.<br /><br />But at heart, \\"The Hunger Games\\" is about one young woman's struggle. Katniss is a struly striking heroine -- she's strong, tough and fiery, as you'd expect of a girl who has been supporting her family, but she has the right amount of vulnerability and kindness. Peeta is a very sweet, sensitive love interest who complements her perfectly, and there's a strong round of supporting characters -- the clever stylist Cinna, the drunken ex-tribute Haymitch, the birdlike Rue, and many others.<br /><br />\\"The Hunger Games\\" is one of those rare books that strikes a deep chord in people's souls -- and it's a beautifully (if oddly) written story with a brilliant heroine. Spellbinding.akes a little getting used to -- she not only writes everything in the first person, but in the present tense. B000E41MRC|4.0|Leni Riefenstahl (1902-2003) began her career as a dancer, progressed to film roles, and ultimately moved into cinematography, editing, and directing.  Adolph Hiter was among her many fans, and although she herself was never a member of the Nazi party, Hitler asked her create a film about it.  Titled VICTORY OF THE FAITH, the 1933 film included significant footage of Ernst Rohm, and when he fell out of favor and was executed the film more or less died with him.  Only one copy survived, and it is rarely seen; even so, it developed the foundation for Riefenstahl's next film, a depiction of the 1934 Nazi Congress in Nuremberg. It was titled TRIUMPH OF THE WILL.<br /><br />Many records perished during World War II, and those pertaining to TRIUMPH OF THE WILL are not excepted.  Although she would later deny that the project was pre-planned in any real sense, Riefenstahl's crew consisted of 172 people, a number that could hardly be managed without considerable advance thought.  It also appears that Riefenstahl went to Nuremberg to have camera tracks and boom shot devices installed in strategic locations long before Hitler arrived.  Reifenstahl also deployed as many as thirty cameras from scene to scene, most them apparently predetermined positions, and one or two scenes have the sense of being actively directed.  Hitler and his entourage were certainly well aware that they were being filmed--and at times repeated portions of their speeches for the sake of a better camera shot. The organizers of the congress were instruced to be as camera-friendly as possible and even went so far as to dig ditches to allow Riefenstahl to get the shots she wanted.  Over the course of about four days, Riefenstahl and her crew shot an incredible sixty-plus hours of film.  Riefenstahl herself edited the film to a run time of two hours; even at this length, historians estimate that THE TRIUMPH OF THE WILL presents film footage showing about thirty thousand people.<br /><br />In later years, Riefenstahl stated that Hilter had asked to make the film because she was apolitical and he wanted a film that would appeal to just such people.  He did not, Riefenstahl said, want a political film--and the film that she delivered is notable for that fact.  Ironically, the very absence of Nazi politics and policy makes them even more obvious than they might have been if they had been included, but Riefenstahl's emphasis is on imagery: impossibly large crowds, masses of flags, endless arrays of torches, incredible bits of scaffolding and rows of standard bearers.  TRIUMPH OF THE WILL is visually staggering to the same degree as such films as INTOLERANCE and THE BATTLE SHIP POTEMKIN.  Her editing is a grand affair, with exceptional tempo; her black and white imagery is extraordinary; her eye is indeed a great one, and although she made less than a dozen films, TRIUMPH OF THE WILL gained Riefenstahl the reputation as one of the greatest film artists of the 20th Century.<br /><br />There is a notion that TRIUMPH OF THE WILL received universal critical acclaim when it opened in 1935.  That is not entirely true.  The film was a great success in Germany, won awards in Paris, and dazzled producers in Hollywood, but it received mixed reviews.  Most were impressed with the imagery and cinematography and editing, but some found the structure commonplace.  And of course, by 1935 the nature of Nazi Germany had become increasingly apparent around the world, and a good many people condemned the film for its visual glorification of the Nazi party.  And these criticisms have continued to this day, and I have to agree that the entire look of the film is essentially a flowering of fascist art.<br /><br />Even so, there is an irony to TRIUMPH OF THE WILL that not even Riefenstahl could have imagined: we know what will happen to these people who parade in the streets, who cheer and wave and dance and parade.  I was repeatedly caught by the young children who smiled and laughed.  How many of them, I wondered, lived?  They danced, many of them willingly, right into the mouth of hell with Adolph Hitler leading the way.  Seen at this level, and balanced against later documentaries such the shocking Army Signal Corps footage of the concentration camps and such feature films such as the 1979 KITTY: RETURN TO AUSCHWITZ--my God, but it is disturbing, deeply disturbing and incredibly sad.<br /><br />There are a great many DVD releases of TRIUMPH OF THE WILL.  This review is of the \\"Special Edition\\" by Synapse Films, and includes a commentary by Dr. Anthony R. Santoro, which I found very erudite but perhaps somewhat dry.  It also includes a short Riefenstahl film, DAY OF FREEDOM, made to placate members of the military who felt TRIUMPH OF THE WILL had given then short shift; it too is remarkable for its imagery.  The elements have not been restored in a major sense, certainly not a digital sense, but the film is sharp enough for us to see the sweat on Hitler's brow, and the sound is quite good.  It is hard to recommend such film, but at the same time I feel everyone should see it at least once.  Evil wears a mask, and very often it is one of remarkable grace.  It is best to know that.<br /><br />GFT, Amazon Reviewer<br />for Nicky, faithful feline companion for a decade, gone before his timef them, I wondered, lived? The driver's love for this family does not abate but only grows when the husbandis beaten badly in the garage of the apartment complex. He owes protection money to the mob. It is here that the Driver breaks his code and helps Irene's husband. Unintentionally, he also familiarizes himself more than he would like with local mobsters such as Bernie Rose (Albert Brooks) and Nino (Ron Perlman).<br /><br />Drive is incredibly well paced and I tend to disagree with all the surrounding clamor that it is slow in the beginning. This is far from the truth. I feel Nicolas was very much in control in how he maintained such a consistent feel of uneasiness throughout the film. He knew exactly when to take it up a notch and smoothly level it down to tame his audience gently. I thought the relationships were plausible enough to service the simple plot and add substance too. I'm not so sure what kind of a connection some critics were looking for but I felt the interactions were realistic. The chemistry was satisfying overall. Ryan Gosling's character was not very multi dimensional and it didn't need to be. He is a loner, plain and simple; no family, no friends and maybe a few enemies ? Ultimately, he is very mysterious but also very explosive, especially when it comes to protecting his neighbor. He is entertaining to watch. The rest of the cast is also serviceable; Albert Brooks pulls of an unapologetic mobster role as well as Ron Perlman. The style and presentation is quite unique. Moreover, the car chases are brilliantly choreographed to perfection; sounds and colors are pleasing to the eyes and ears and the violence is appropriately delivered. Nicolas reignites a once dominate American auto industry in the way he presents these distasteful and bulky hunks of metal; Ford and Chrysler should pay Nicolas royalties for making their cars look so darn good.<br /><br />I never overlook a film's score and in this particular case, Cliff Martinez scores a masterpiece from start to finish. Martinez weaves together an electronic 80's pop soundtrack that dominates the opening and ending scenes and adds his own personal and eery flare that is so central to Ryan Gosling's character. He enhances the desolation that is so prevalent in the Los Angeles landscape. The Driver's internal feelings are remarkably correlated to every vibrating moan that is released from Martinez's dominate usage of the synthesizer.  The subtle but eery sounds create a quite atmosphere of curiosity and danger in this beautiful and highly stylized film.

B00000JMOF|5.0|FRANKENSTEIN<br /><br />Few monsters are so recognizable as James Whale's in Frankenstein as played by Boris Karloff and make-up artist Jack Pierce.  But as great as that monster is, the movie is wonderful in other respects--the script, acting, set design--all make this one of the most well rounded horror films ever made and a continual joy to watch.<br /><br />Whale's adaptation strays quite a bit from the book, so it isn't wrong to say that his version of Frankenstein is somewhat original.  In the film version, the Doctor, aided by his deformed and loyal assistant Fritz, embarks on a sinister plan to reanimate dead flesh into a living being.  It's a noble plan and hits upon an age old fault of men--pride and arrogance.  Grave robbing is bad enough, but the good Doctor touches on the blasphemous, declaring in the infamously censored scene when he yells \\"Now I know what it feels like to be God!\\"  Never the less, he brings the creature to life only to find it less than satisfactory and under some peer pressure agrees to destroy the beast.  Things go wrong (naturally) and the Doctor finds himself pitted against the creature in a life or death struggle.<br /><br />What's great about the movie is Whale's adherence to Shelly's humanistic approach to the story.  All the characters are very real and sympathetic.  Even the lowly Fritz whose delights include grave robbing and tormenting Frankenstein's poor creature evokes feeling from the viewer.  The tale itself seems to be one big tragic story.  Frankenstein, despite his faults and lack of better judgment, is still human and deserving of our pity.  The monster takes center stage in this department.  He's done nothing wrong and asked just for love and understanding, but receives instead torment and pain.  In many ways the monster is the best representative of the human condition, a man trapped in a harsh and unforgiving world, whose creator abandons him, and like one who is scorned, the monster seeks to destroy his creator.<br /><br />There are numerous memorable visuals in this movie.  The most obvious is the laboratory scene when Frankenstein brings his creature to life.  Most people overlook it, but a lot of work and thought went into creating the \\"mad-scientist laboratory\\" complete with a range of instruments with no real purpose other than to look exciting.  The monster's first appearance as he walks into the room backwards and then the close-up, all done in nearly complete silence accentuate the suspense.  Then there is the finale at the windmill between the two main characters, facing one another as the whole place incinerates around them.<br /><br />The acting, while seemingly simple, was actually pretty in depth.  The three persons who stand out are Colin Clive (the Doctor), Karloff, and Dwight Fry (Fritz).  They are an odd ensemble and not only do they all give great performances, but they don't have a single dull moment between them.  Some people criticize Karloff because his role is so drab, but his version of the monster is in complete contrast with that in the novel and in some ways, a bit more complex.  Remember, in the novel the monster is actually an intelligent and physical marvel whereas Karloff's creature seems mentally dull, uncoordinated, incapable of speech or spiritual substance.  One can feel great pity for the confused beast while simultanously loathing it as the abomination that it is.  Clive  definied the classic image of the mad scientist, his line \\"It's alive!\\" is immortal.  Fry, too, defined the hunchbacked assistant as no other could.<br /><br />Another aspect worth mentioning is how the movie flows.  It moves around very nicely so you're constantly engaged in the story.  Whale was a master at introducing spectacle to break up periods of dialogue but without going overboard.  It's also nice to see how the characters develop and never become dull or unbelievable.  Frankenstein's range of emotions go from ambitious scientist to humbled man in such a way that is totally compelling.<br /><br />Frankenstein is overall just a jewel of a horror movie.  It never gets old and will always stand out as a solidly constructed movie.  It's effects and messages are just as potent today as they were in 1931 and it features some famous horror actors at their prime.  The very best movie from the genres very best director.hat is totally compelling.<br /><br />Frankenstein is overall just a jewel of a horror movie.  It never gets old and will always stand out as a solidly constructed movie.  It's effects and messages are just as potent today as they were in 1931 and it features some famous horror actors at their prime.  The very best movie from the genres very best director.

0307352145|5.0|Every once in a while, a book comes along that just knocks your socks off. Quiet by Susan Cain is one of those books. I originally ordered the book thinking that I would us it to help out some of the shier students in my classroom. The last thing I thought of was the book helping me. But I guess life is just full of surprises like that. And who thought that a psychology book would actually help someone besides a psychologist?    Susan Cain digs deep into her own psyche and experiences, along with a deep well of studies - each chapter is packed with interesting data from various psychological studies - and stories of some of the great introverts of our time. A few of these individuals you may have heard of: Gandhi, Rosa Parks, Steve Wozniak, Warren Buffet, Lewis Carroll, and many others. Oh...also some guy named Einstein (You may have heard of him.). Some of them changed their financial futures, and some changed the financial futures of others, while some where content to do something silly, like change the world. Quiet: The Power of Introverts in a World That Can't Stop Talking is an incredible look    into the thoughts, feelings, and actions of the introvert. If you're not sure which of those you are, then definitely get the book. If you are sure of what you are...definitely get the book. Introversion takes many forms. I'm not sure if it's exactly one of those snowflake scenarios, but maybe (or maybe it's just still snowing in April in Idaho, so snowflakes are on the mind). At any rate, if you are an introvert, work with an introvert, are the parent of an introvert, the spouse of an introvert, or you just want to know what an introvert is, then check this book out.    Cain's point is not to say that introverts are better or more necessary than introverts. Rather, she makes the point that we need to find a way to better access and develop our introverts. From business, to schools, to the little piece of introvert that lies within us all - okay, I made that last partup myself - we need to be intentional about the \\"shy\\" kid who sits in the back of the classroom. Oftentimes this shyness can be seen as \\"weakness\\" or a lack of social understanding. And this may well be true, but being slow, thoughtful, or methodical is not to be \\"`weak.\\" Rather, it is a different way to interact with the stimuli in around you.    There is far too much to say about the depth and grace with which Cain is able to dive into this incredible topic. As she says, anywhere from one in three to one in two are introverts. So let's stop talking over the top of them and hear what they have to say. When I say \\"them\\" I mean \\"us.\\" I'm an introvert, loud and proud...or quiet and pensive. I personally learned a great deal about myself from this book that I will apply on a daily basis. How often can you say that about a book, eh? If you have any form of social anxiety, or know someone who does, this is definitely your book. Buy it. Read it. Pass it along.    If you want to check out a better synopsis than what my meager review can represent, check out Susan Cain talking about her journey at TEDtalks. If you're not drawn in, then I'll never bother you again.    [...]  Introverts of the world unite! But quietly...I'm sure we'll be meeting in a library.    I received this book free from in order to review it. There is no requirement to give a positive review. Avoid purchasing it if you do not like being challenged by the books you read; basically, if you like walking away from mirrors forgetting what you looked like.

B004X80QNG|5.0|Over the weekend I finally devoted time to really learning Pocket Informant. My setup is as follows: rooted Android 2.3 Tmobile MyTouch 3G Slide phone, Outlook 2010 for Windows (not Exchange), Google calendar (for calendar items only), and Toodledo for Tasks. Outlook, under the hood, handles calendar and tasks differently, and in ways that drive 3rd party app developers crazy. That's why it's best to let ToodleDo handle tasks and Google for calendar. PI brings both together in a variety of useful displays. The sync glue that makes this all work is an arson software called gsync. It's currently costs $19 dollars. Gsync syncs Outlook tasks to ToodleDo, and PI syncs with ToodleDo (free version is all I need). Gsync syncs calendar items to Google calendar, and PI syncs with Google calendar. Gsync also handles contact syncing to Google with the phone then automatically syncing contacts from the Google cloud. For a little over $30 (PI + Gsync) you get a bullet proof sync setup--at least that's how it's been for me. I assume you already have Outlook. The PI documentation could be better but spend a few minutes experimenting with PI and you'll do fine. One other recommendation is to get the Outlook 2010<br />GTD Setup document from the David Allen website. This doc really helped me implement GTD on both Outlook and PI. The danger any GTD developer faces is dealing with the abundance of engineering type personalities that GTD attracts. They all think a GTD product is lacking because it doesn't include every obscure feature under the sun. Same reaction if they need to combine one product with another at an additional cost e.g. PI with Gsync. You can endlessly spend your time trying to create that perfect GTD setup (I've been there), or you can start using the combination of tools as I've outlined and avoid getting stuck in a tweaking morass. Hopefully I don't come across as a shill for any of these products. Rather I wanted to outline my GTD solution that's working well for me. I have not tried PI on my Kindle Fire yet.

B000066C6F|5.0|Ultimately critics of the movie 'Perfect' may well come to understand this film as I came to see it upon walking out of the theater on opening night: not as a relic of mid-80's cheese and bad script writing, but actually as a stunning artistic career exploration that may well be regarded as the fait d'accompli of the Travolta opus!! Let me explain.<br /><br />You must challenge yourself to go back to that very uncomfortable period of time (those old enough to remember), to the time between the disco-studded leisure suit success of Travolta's early years and the action-packed genre of his most recent blow up/shoot em up flicks. In this inter-modal time period you will find a self-doubting Travolta who most people believed - as did the illuminati of the East Coast entertainment media - that he was at the nadir of his career. His entourage had long since abandoned him. Entertainment writers (to the degree they paid any attention at all to this fading 70's icon) panned his every move. His agent wasn't calling him back, and choice male lead roles were going to the likes of Stallone and the puerile Tom Cruise. So Travolta probably figured, why accept these infantile roles that are unpalatable and fake to begin with? Why not strike it out on his own and do the signature roles he was afraid to tell his agent he really wanted to pursue? And what emerged from this burst of artistic self indulgence were instant classic films like 'Look Who's Talking' and 'Look Who's Talking 2'. He wasn't being pushed by some Hollywood big shot to sign on to the next blood bath (ala Stalone) or coerced by the love-starved public to prostrate himself upon the alter of a tweener romance (ala Cruise). It is within this context that we find the movie 'Perfect'. In other words...it is the rarest, purest form of an unadulterated, unpretentiousness John Travolta you will ever see committed to celluloid. It is the un-Tom Cruise. And it is very revealing.<br /><br />In 'Perfect' Travolta plays a hard bitten reporter pursing a story on, of all things, health clubs. He encounters Jaime Lee Curtis, who doesn't immediately fall for his machismo charms, but you just know she will be incapable of resisting by about minute 63. So you know what he has to do. Go undercover. Deep undercover. His aim: to explore the health club sub-culture, burn some joules of energy and win the girl. Along the way, of course, we're treated to a masculinity redefining experience of Travolta in aerobic tights that challenges every viewer - man or woman, gay or straight - to experience the maximum threshold of uncomfortablilty known to human kind. It's off the charts. Dear reader, are you not seeing through this paper thin veil of a plot to the deeper interior? Come with me through the looking glass. This is what Edgar Allan Poe called, \\"the hideous dropping off of the veil.\\" For it is within this plot that we find Travolta crying out for acceptance, to be loved once more as a Danny Zuco or the guy he played in Saturday Night Fever, but not really knowing how to go back there. His only recourse is to make US - you and I the viewing public- see ourselves in his character, to experience the comfortableness that must surely be the province of an actor at the cross roads of his career. Yet, it is only by exploring this character was Travolta able to emerge from it new and introspective, to draw new courage for the next phase of his career.<br /><br />Have we judged Travolta too harshly in this movie? I suspect so. \\"Travolta in tights\\" is all we heard from the critic (yes singular - there just weren't that many critics back then). They said it would be his last pic. They were already writing the obit on his career. They didn't know at the time that Travolta was already picking out fabric swatches for the interior of his G5, that he had his sights set on reclaiming his place atop the list of Hollywood A-listers. While we were laughing at him dancing around making ridiculous contortions on the studiofloor, he was looking back into that camera mind banging us.<br /><br />Definately time for the studio to release the Blu-Ray version. Maybe in time for the 30th anniversary. Here's to John Travolta who must certainly be considered for a place atop the pantheon of aerobic greatness along side Jane Fonda and Richard Simmons. And to an even greater accomplishment by crossing the doldrums of his career and emerging even stronger thanks to critical roles in movies like 'Perfect'.

1613822634|5.0|\\"Handsome, clever and rich\\" is how Emma is introduced to us, and a happy, carefree existence she leads, with very little to worry her other than idle gossip. The youngest of two sisters, Emma lives alone with her father, doting on him, after her sister Isabella marries. Their mother is long deceased, and Emma has grown up with a kindly governess, Miss Taylor, who bestows strong motherly affection on her.<br />Set in 18th century rural England, the novel affords us a picturesque, detailed view of the daily tenets of English life at the time, complete with carriages, gowns, housekeepers and social traditions. Austen weaves a delicious web of Emma's life and that of her friends in Highbury, where they live. Mr. Woodhouse, Emma's father, is a gentle, kind man with an excessively considerate compassion to others that often borders on paranoia. He is constantly afraid of catching cold, or falling ill, and lectures those around him incessantly on the need for precaution. We learn of Mr. Knightley, a long-time, close neighbor of the family, whose brother is married to Isabella, and of the Westons, Bates, and Perrys, all families of the area, as they intermingle in Emma's world.<br />Harriet, a girl of less social advantage, is taken by Emma under her wing. Emma's favorite hobby is matchmaking, and we watch her make one blunder after the next to poor Harriet. When Robert Martin, a young farmer, proposes to her friend, Emma retaliates very sharply, advising Harriet against marrying him and \\"falling into lower circumstance.\\" Harriet is miserable, but appears to be convinced. Mr. Knightley, ever present in Emma's life and home, scolds her sharply for her interference, but Emma stands her ground defiantly, insisting that she knows what is best for Harriet.<br />When a Mr. Elton appears on the scene, pouring lavish attentions onto them, Emma is convinced of his being far superior to Mr. Martin, and does all in her power to coax Harriet into returning his feelings. All the while,she is smugly telling Mr. Knightley that she predicts a far better outcome for her friend than his preference of Mr. Martin. Harriet becomes attached to Mr. Elton, and all is going to plan, when Emma receives a tumultuous shock: Mr. Elton asks for her own hand in marriage. Emma, horrified, asks him about his feelings for Harriet, but he denies vehemently, saying that all his advances were meant towards Emma! Our heroine then sinks into utter guilt and mortification, watching Harriet's heart break due to her own wheedling and landing her in this mess.<br />Mr. Elton wastes no time; he soon marries another rich woman, obviously keen to secure a fortune. Meanwhile, Emma's attention is caught by Mr. Frank Churchill, a recent arrival to Highbury, but she comfortably assures herself of her immunity to love and marriage. She flirts with him, but does not entertain any serious ideas towards him--only to find herself duped, again, when his secret engagement to her neighbor is revealed.<br />Overwhelmed by all her blunders, Emma is feeling a great deal of confusion and remorse, but there is a final blow that she is unprepared for. Out of the blue, Harriet shares her new feelings for Mr. Knightley with her, and her hope that these feelings may be returned.<br />Emma's world crashes at that moment. She panics and feels extremely agitated, which suddenly leads her to realize her own love for Mr. Knightley, a love unknown and unacknowledged by her. As she stares into herself, she reflects on his constant presence in her life, her attachment to him, her extreme care for his opinion. The thought of losing him is too painful to bear, and Emma, for the first time in the story, is plunged into total misery. But the tables turn yet again. As she awaits his breaking the news to her, of his attachment to Harriet, Mr. Knightley comes forth with a powerful declaration of love for Emma, a love he has had for years. In a very touching scene that causes the reader's heart to soar, Mr. Knightley, normally not a man of many words, pours his feelings to Emma in anguish. He asks her to marry him, with a pained conviction that he will be refused. Emma is overjoyed, assures his troubles away, accepts without a second thought.<br />Amidst her shock, and just as she is dealing with the conflicting emotions of her own extreme happiness, and great mortification for Harriet, Mr. Knightley saves the day by encouraging Mr. Martin to approach Harriet again. The girl's feelings for him, which had never ceased, finally prevail, and the couple are united.<br />Despite her haughty airs and egotism, Emma is \\"faultless despite all her faults\\" in the eyes of Mr. Knightley, and we can't help liking her, too, for she is always trying to do good, and her heart is in the right place. Mr. Knightley himself, kind, generous, sincere and honorable--a close reminder of Mr. Darcy--wins us over, and we breathlessly wait for things to work out between him and Emma. The author, with a remarkable talent for making us hold our breath, turning the tables and providing unexpected turns, concludes the book with happy endings for all, leaving us smiling.<br />Austen's language, two centuries ago, is as delicious as the novel itself, the quaint writing taking us on a foray into older English and its idioms, structures and expressions. One of my favorite novels, Emma is a delight to read, from start to finish, and a story that captivates the imagination right until the last page.

0525423656|2.0|In Crossed, the sequel to Ally Condie's Matched, the story picks up to where the reader left off. Ky is working in a labor camp in the Outer Provinces and Cassia is getting moved around every couple of months on work assignments. Both characters are desperate to find each other. When Cassia gets transported to the Outer Provinces, she is hopeful that she will finally be able to find Ky. However, she finds that he has run away from the labor camp and has disappeared into dangerous and mysterious canyons, where the members of the resistance are rumored to be living. Cassia is invested in finding Ky, as well as joining the Rising that supposedly lives in the canyon. However, Ky, while desperate to find Cassia, is reluctant to join the Rising because of his own past.<br /><br />To get the perspectives of Cassia and Ky, the narration switches from Cassia to Ky every chapter. Sometimes I found this a little bit confusing, because both sounded incredibly similar. I frequently had to go back to the beginning of the chapter to see who's POV I was reading. However, the upside to this is that as a reader you can get into the heads of both Cassia and Ky. Both characters provide different insights into not only themselves but also the secondary characters. For example, Xander only appears once in the book, but he is mentioned throughout as both characters think about him. Thus, trying to keep the love triangle alive. Ky knows a secret that Xander shares, but is unwilling to share it with Cassia. Other characters that are introduced include Vick, Eli,a boy who reminds Ky and Cassia of Bram, and Indie, a girl who Ky does not quite trust.<br /><br />This book suffers from what I call The Sequel Disappointment. There is always so much anticipation of when the sequel comes out, that it is hard to read the sequel and have it be as Knock-Your-Socks-Off good as its predecessor. I am not sure whether it is the anticipation, the standard of the first book, or what, but I was disappointedwith this book. It can be noted that The Sequel Disappointment is also a close relative to the Book to Movie Paradigm.<br /><br />Crossed for me was just very slow from the beginning. Both characters are in the desert pining for each other, which frankly just does not move the plot forwards. The first two hundred pages of the book is about Ky and Cassia looking for each other in the desert. It gets old fast. Like sands in the hourglass, nobody wants to endure long periods of time watching that. There were several opportunities for action or plot thickening, however, they action was told and not described and they were cut short. The characters had something that they both wanted, but because of the chopped nature of the potential actions sequences, there was not overarching tension to pull the plot along. There are a couple of last minute attempts of surprise later in the book, but at that point it is a bit too little, too late.<br /><br />To conclude, Crossed does not live up to Matched. It is yet another disappointing sequel that generates very little excitement or reasons to keep reading.
B0073XORLU|5.0|Jethro Tull singer/songwriter Ian Anderson's new solo album Thick As a Brick 2 (or TAAB 2 as he calls it) is a must for Jethro Tull fans.<br />Having been a fan of the original 1972 Jethro Tull classic Thick As a Brick (which became the band's first US #1 album in 1972 upon its release) since I first heard the album on the radio back in the 1990s (and my reason I got into Jethro Tull's music), I was surprised that a sequel to the classic album was coming out earlier this year. Then when I saw it was to be released as a solo album from Ian, I said \\"who would fill the shoes of Martin Barre's guitar?\\". Turns out it's Florian Ophale. Then who would take over Jeffrey Hammond's role on bass guitar? It is David Goodier (who has been in Jethro Tull since 2006). Who would play the keyboards that John Evan did brilliantly on the original? John O'Hara (also been a Tull member since 2006). Finally, who would drum in the seat of Barriemore Barlow?\\" That role is taken over by Scott Hammond.<br />Over the years, alot of bands have done sequel albums to either classic albums or albums in their catalog that were either superb (KISS Alive II, Led Zeppelin 2, Led Zeppelin 3, Led Zeppelin IV, Van Halen II, Peter Gabriel (Scratch (Peter Gabriel 2), Melt (Peter Gabriel 3) and Security (Peter Gabriel 4)) or downright terrible (Queensryche's Operation : Mindcrime II, Meat Loaf's Bat Out of Hell III, Metallica's Re-Load and Alice Cooper's Welcome To My Nightmare 2). Luckily, Ian falls into the former with TaaB 2 as this is his best work he has done as a solo artist and has done since the 1989 Jethro Tull album Rock Island.<br />In this day and age of the single download and soundbite music garbage thrown by the musical floosies (Lady Gaga, Rihanna, Beyonce, Britney Spears, Christina Aguilera and Katy Perry) and crap rap (LMFAO, Eminem, Kanye West, Jay Z and the ilk) of the world, a concept album is seen as old fashioned and also not acceptable in this current music climate (but someone forgot to tell that to Judas Priest who did Nostradamus in 2008 and also Ian Anderson). What does Ian Anderson do? He decides to come up with a What-If's, Maybes and Might Have Beens concept in the lyrics to see what happened to the hero from the original Thick As a Brick, the eight year old child prodigy Gerald Bostock (now aged 48).<br />The intro of the album reprises the riff that linked the two halves to Thick As Brick which then goes into a great rocker out of \\"From a Pebble Thrown\\". \\"Pebbles Instrumental\\" is a great piece. We follow with \\"Might-have-beens\\" which speaks of situations Gerald may be in today. The two pieces which sees Gerald as a banker \\"Upper Sixth Lower Shark\\" and \\"Banker Bets, Banker Wins\\" are excellent and fits in the story. The story that sees Gerald as Homeless is represented in the rockers \\"Swing It Far\\" and \\"Adrift and Confounded\\" which are superb. Gerald as Military Man begins with \\"Old School Song\\" which reminds of the \\"I come down from the upper clouds\\" part from the original TaaB. Then it goes to \\"Wootton Basset Town\\" which is a superb piece of music.<br />Gerald as Choirster section is comprised of the brilliant \\"Power and Spirit\\" and \\"Give Till It Hurts\\" which sees if Gerald had become a Jimmy Swaggart type. Gerald as A Most Ordinary Man is summed up by the excellent \\"Cosy Corner\\" and \\"Shunt and Shuffle\\" which musically reminds me of \\"Locomotive Breath\\". Next is the epic \\"A Change of Horses\\" which is a great piece. The 22 Mulberry Walk is summed up in \\"Confessional\\" and the brilliant \\"Kismet in Suburbia\\". We close the album with \\"What-ifs, Maybes, Might-Have-Beens\\" which musically serves as a superb recap to an excellent album and with the outro from the original to bring the album full circle.<br />Thick As a Brick 2 is already in my running of Best Rock Album of 2012 and joins the likes of David Gilmour's On an Island, Rush's Snakes and Arrows, Dennis DeYoung's One Hundred Years From Now, Iron Maiden's The Final Frontier on the listof Superb New Albums by Veteran Rockers. It may not get the sales nor accolades but in my heart it is a brilliant album.<br />RECOMMENDED!of Superb New Albums by Veteran Rockers. It may not get the sales nor accolades but in my heart it is a brilliant album.<br />RECOMMENDED!

B007J4T2G8|3.0|I've read a lot of reviews for this book/series. And I've come to the conclusion that most folks are either going to *love* the 50 Shades series, or they're going to loathe it. Having read my fair share of fanfiction, while also getting my degree in English lit, I've seen both sides of the writing coin and have to say that this book has the makings of a *great* novel, with a great romantic pair akin to Romeo and his Juliet, and Catherine to her Heathcliff... the *makings*. This was a hastily released book/series. It was as if the author had the first draft leaked and just left it like that. Marks of greatness are there in the fatal flaws of Christian, the supreme innocence of Ana, hints at delicious complexities and satisfying resolution. However, more than just Christian has fatal flaws, sadly.<br /><br />The amount of repetition is almost embarrassing. And I'm not just talking about the sheer overload of sexual encounters described in this book, of which there are far too many (can there be too many you ask? YES!), but also of the turns of phrase that are beaten into the text until they're nothing but a bloody pulp. \\"Fair point well made\\", and \\"don't bite your lip\\" come to mind. Trimming these items down so that they aren't showing up every two or three pages, but often enough to create a rapport between the two main characters, would make this book a 4 or 5 star piece, easily.<br /><br />And can I simply point out that no woman \\"comes\\" as easily nor as often as Anastasia? I think the ease at which she orgasms could be considered a medical *disorder* that should be checked out by a doctor. Make sure that poor girl doesn't have some sort of very pleasurable cancer or something. It's embarrassing.<br /><br />Like I said though, these are hiccups that could have been smoothed out with further revision. Sadly, that was not done, and we have what we have. It's rough, but for those of us with an imagination, we can see where the book could go, and create satisfying corrections for ourselves to fill in the blanks. And for those without any imagination, well, just enjoy the sex scenes: there's a lot of them.

B00701QVVY|5.0|So often glowing reviews are put out there by long time fans of a band who feel that their heroes can do no wrong.  Metallica could fart and belch into a microphone and there would be people lining up to praise it simply because it carried the Metallica name.  This is not one such review.  I'm not a long time, die hard fan of Overkill.  I've heard all of their catalog and I own about half of it. It takes a lot for me to put a review of something up here, so these words are probably as objective as you can get.  And now...<br /><br />Consistency, thy name might as well be Overkill. In a career spanning more than 25 (!!!) years and a staggering 17 albums, the east coast thrashers have never enjoyed the same amount of mainstream success as many of their peers (Metallica, Megadeth, Anthrax, Slayer, etc.), but then again, they've never sold out either.  When one considers that even the mighty Slayer farted out duds like Diabolus in Musica and God Hates Us All, this kind of track record is all the more amazing.  Even on an album like I Hear Black (which some fans--not me-- regard as sub-par for flirting with doomy tempos and some groove metal elements) is still a far cry from the MTV-friendly cack that Metallica and Megadeth were putting out at that time.  In fact, I Hear Black, like Testament's The Ritual has actually aged fairly well.  But I digress.<br /><br />Like Overkill's previous album Ironbound, The Electric Age offers no surprises, musically speaking.  This is pure, heads-down, fist-in-the-air thrash metal. There are no prog flights of fancy, no extended acoustic numbers, and Blitz doesn't try his hand at rapping.  And thank the metal gods for that. The only surprise is that after endless lineup changes and label shuffles, Overkill is just as good as they were way back in the Years of Decay era.  In fact, I think they're even better. Link and Tailer are arguably the best guitarists Overkill has had, and Lipnicki is without a doubt the best drummer. The production here is also top notch, taming some of the metallic clang in D.D. Verni's bass so that it sits more comfortably in the mix.<br /><br />There are no bad tracks on The Electric Age.  Literally every single one of them is a winner, but there are a few standouts.  Electric Rattlesnake, with its mid-song detour into Sabbath territory, is a smorgasbord of tasty riffs. All Over But the Shouting has an appropriately shout-along chorus. Come and Get It has a pounding intro that builds to a furious thrasher.  Bring the Hammer Down had a mid-paced swagger that is downright infectious. Actually, each and every song has at least one part that makes you want to crush a beer and stomp around like a madman.<br /><br />To sum up: this is seriously good thrash metal. As good as Worship Music is, this is the album that Anthrax only wishes they could make.  And it goes without saying that it's head and shoulders above the bloated turkey that is Megadeth's Thirteen. The only thing that keeps me from declaring this the thrash metal album of the year is the fact that both Kreator and Testament still have releases on the horizon. Go ahead and click the Buy Now button.  You can thank me later.

The image of this metropolis during the 1930s was interwoven with chronic political struggles between communists and nationalists, the ascendancy and recession of foreign powers and warlords, and the presence of Japanese militarism. The historical reconstruction of a murder case of a 19-year old English woman in January of 1937 has unveiled how justice could be distorted and trampled by a group of people from the privileged class.<br /><br />In this book, what might make readers squirm is that the murder suspects, diplomats, and members of the justice community were well-educated people and/or enjoyed excellent social reputation. Readers can get access to [...] that includes an audio walking tour of the major sites, a map of old Peking, photographs, and original news clippings of the investigation. This book is highly recommended to readers who are interested in Holmes-or Eco-style detective novel and history of China during the 1930s.
